                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">سَآءَ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, (Lth, M, Msb, K,) aor. <foreign lang="ar">يَسُوْءُ</foreign>, (Lth, Msb,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">سَوْءٌ</foreign>, (Lth, M,) or <foreign lang="ar">سَوَآءٌ</foreign>, like <foreign lang="ar">سَحَابٌ</foreign>, (K,) [but the former is that which is commonly known,] <hi rend="ital">It</hi> (a thing, Lth, M) <hi rend="ital">was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, evil, bad, abominable, foul, unseemly, unsightly,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">ugly.</hi> (Lth, M, Msb, K.) It is used in this sense, (IKt, TA,) or [rather] is like <foreign lang="ar">بِئْسَ</foreign>, (Bd, Jel,) in the Kur [xvii. 34], where it is said, <foreign lang="ar">سَآءَ سَبِيلًا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Evil,</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">is it as a way of acting</hi>]: (IKt, Bd, Jel, TA:) which is like the saying, <foreign lang="ar">سَآءَ هٰذَا مَذْهَبًا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Evil,</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">is this as a way of acting</hi> or <hi rend="ital">believing,</hi> &amp;c.]: the noun being in the accus. case as a specificative. (IKt, TA.) And so in the saying, <foreign lang="ar">سَآءَ مَا فَعَلَ فُلَانٌ صَنِيعًا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Evil,</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">as an action, is that which such a one has done</hi>]. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  One says also, <foreign lang="ar">سُؤْتُ بِهِ ظَنًّا</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n21120-1" target="أَسَأْتُ" n="1" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>بِهِ الظَّنَّ</foreign>, [lit. <hi rend="ital">I was evil in opinion respecting him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">I made the opinion respecting him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it, to be evil,</hi> each virtually meaning <hi rend="ital">I held,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">formed, an evil opinion respecting him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it,</hi>] the noun being determinate, with the article <foreign lang="ar">ال</foreign>, in the latter case, (ISk, S, Msb, TA,) because it is an objective complement, for the verb is trans., (IB, TA,) and the noun being indeterminate in the former case, (IB, Msb, TA,) because it is in the accus. case as a specificative; (IB, TA;) but some allow it to be indeterminate after   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n21120-2" target="أَسَأْتُ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, which is here the <hi rend="ital">contr. of</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">أَحْسَنْتُ</foreign>. (Msb.)       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  It is also trans.: (Lth, TA:) you say, <foreign lang="ar">سَآءَهُ</foreign>, (S, M, K,) aor. <foreign lang="ar">يَسُوْؤُهُ</foreign>, (S,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">سَوْءٌ</foreign> (S, M, K) and <foreign lang="ar">سُوْءٌ</foreign>, with damm also, (TA, [and said to be an inf. n. in the Ksh and by Bd in ii. 46, but as it is not mentioned as an inf. n. in the S nor in the M nor in the K, but is expressly said in all these to be a subst., I think that is should be rejected, or regarded as a quasi-inf. n. like <foreign lang="ar">كَلَامٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">ثَوَابٌ</foreign> &amp;c.,]) <foreign lang="ar">سَوَآةٌ</foreign> (K) and <foreign lang="ar">سَوَآءَةٌ</foreign> (AZ, M, K) and <foreign lang="ar">سَوَاىءِيَةٌ</foreign> (S, M, K,) of the measure <foreign lang="ar">فَعَالِيَةٌ</foreign>, like <foreign lang="ar">عَلَانِيَةٌ</foreign> (Kh, S, M,) and <foreign lang="ar">سَوَايَةٌ</foreign>, (S, M, K,) which is a contraction of that next preceding, (Kh, S, M,) and <foreign lang="ar">مَسَآءٌ</foreign> (M, K) and <foreign lang="ar">مَسَآءَةٌ</foreign>, (S, M, K,) originally <foreign lang="ar">مَسْوَأَةٌ</foreign>, (Har p. 81,) and <foreign lang="ar">مَسَائِيَةٌ</foreign>, which is originally <foreign lang="ar">مَسَاوِئَةٌ</foreign>, (Kh, S, M, K,) and <foreign lang="ar">مَسَايَةٌ</foreign>, (S, M, K,) which is a contraction of that next preceding, (Kh, S,) and <foreign lang="ar">مَسَائِيَّةٌ</foreign>, (M, K,) this last written in the L with two <foreign lang="ar">ى</foreign> s, [i. e. <foreign lang="ar">مَسَاييَِةٌ</foreign>,] (TA,) [<hi rend="ital">He did evil to him;</hi>] <hi rend="ital">he did to him that which he disliked,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">hated;</hi> (M, K;) <hi rend="ital">he displeased, grieved,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">vexed, him; contr. of</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">سَرَّهُ</foreign>. (S.) One says, <foreign lang="ar">سُؤْتُ الرَّجُلَ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">I displeased, grieved,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">vexed, the man by what he saw</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">experienced</hi>] <hi rend="ital">from me.</hi> (S.) And <foreign lang="ar">أَرَدْتُ مَسَآءَتَكَ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">مَسَائِيَتَكَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I desired to displease, grieve,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">vex, thee</hi>]. (Lth, TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">إِنَّ اللَّيْلَ طَوِيلٌ وَلَا يَسُؤْ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بَالُهُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Verily the night is long, and may the state thereof not displease, grieve,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">vex,</hi> me]: meaning <foreign lang="ar">لَا يَسُؤْنِى بَالُهُ</foreign>; and expressing a prayer. (Lh, M. [In the TA, in the place of <foreign lang="ar">بَالُهُ</foreign> is put <foreign lang="ar">ما له</foreign>; as though meaning <foreign lang="ar">مَا لَهُ مِنَ الحَوَادِثِ</foreign> or the like, i. e. <hi rend="ital">its events,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">accidents,</hi> &amp;c.]) And <foreign lang="ar">لَهُ عِنْدِي</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">مَا سَآءَهُ وَنَآءَهُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I have, belonging to him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">I owe him, what grieved him, and oppressed him by its weight</hi>], and <foreign lang="ar">مَا يَسُوْؤُهُ وَيَنُوْؤُهُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">what does,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">will, grieve him,</hi> &amp;c.]. (S.) <foreign lang="ar">تَرَكَ مَا يَسُوْؤُهُ وَيَنُوْؤُهُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He left,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">has left, what will grieve him, and oppress him by its weight,</hi> on the day of judgment, by the responsibility that it has imposed upon him,] is a prov., said of him who has left his property to his heirs. (Meyd, TA.) It is said that El-Mahboobee was possessed of riches; and when death visited him, he desired to make a testament; so it was said to him, “ What wilt thou write? ” and he answered, “ Write ye, 'Such a one,' meaning himself, 'has left what will grieve him, and oppress him by its weight:' ” i. e., property which his heirs will devour, while the burden thereof will remain upon him. (Meyd, TA.) [See also 4.]          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  One says also, <foreign lang="ar">سُؤْتُ وَجْهَ فُلَانٍ</foreign>, aor. <foreign lang="ar">أَسُوْؤُهُ</foreign>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">مَسَآءَةٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">مَسَائِيَةٌ</foreign>, (Lth, TA,) <hi rend="ital">i. q.</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">قَبَحْتُهُ</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">I said, May God remove the person</hi> (lit. <hi rend="ital">the face</hi>) <hi rend="ital">of such a one far from good,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">prosperity,</hi> &amp;c.]. (TA. [It is said in a copy of the M, that <foreign lang="ar">سُؤْتُ لَهُ وَجْهَهُ</foreign> means <foreign lang="ar">قَبَّحْتُهُ</foreign>: but I think that the right explanation is <foreign lang="ar">قَبَحْتُهُ</foreign>, without tesh-deed, meaning <hi rend="ital">I said to him,</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">قَبَحَ ٱللّٰهُ وَجْهَكَ</foreign>: see art. <foreign lang="ar">قبح</foreign>.])    </entryFree>26:T670,<entryFree id="n21121" key="سوّأ" type="main">

                     <itype>2</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">سوّأ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> [<hi rend="ital">He corrupted,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">marred</hi>]. You say, <foreign lang="ar">سَوِّ وَلَا تُسَوِّئْ</foreign>

(A'Obeyd, S.)       <foreign lang="ar">لا <ref cref="n21353-5" target="سَيَّمَا" n="5" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> is a dial. var. thereof, (Msb,) a compound of <foreign lang="ar">سِىّ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">مَا</foreign>, denoting exception: (S:) one says, <foreign lang="ar">لَا سِيَّمَا زَيْدٍ</foreign>, i. e. <foreign lang="ar">لَا مِثْلَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">زَيْدٍ</foreign> [lit. <hi rend="ital">There is not the like of Zeyd;</hi> virtually, and generally, meaning <hi rend="ital">above all Zeyd,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">especially Zeyd</hi>]; <foreign lang="ar">مَا</foreign> being redundant: and <foreign lang="ar">لا سيّما</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">زَيْدٌ</foreign> also; like as one says, <foreign lang="ar">دَعْ مَا زَيْدٌ</foreign>: (M, K:) [J says,] with respect to the case of the noun following <foreign lang="ar">ما</foreign>, there are two ways: you may make <foreign lang="ar">مَا</foreign> to be in the place of <foreign lang="ar">الَّذِى</foreign>, and mean that an inchoative is to be understood, [namely, <foreign lang="ar">هو</foreign> or the like,] and put the noun that you mention in the nom. case as the enunciative; thus you may say, <foreign lang="ar">جَآءَنِى القَوْمُ لَا سِيَّمَا أَخُوكَ</foreign>, meaning <foreign lang="ar">لَا سِىَّ الَّذِى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">هُوَ أَخُوكَ</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">The people,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">party, came to me,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">there was not the like of him who is thy brother;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">above all,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">especially, he who is thy brother</hi>]: (S, TA: [thus in a copy of the S: in other copies of the same, and in the TA, for <foreign lang="ar">سِىَّ</foreign>, <foreign lang="ar">سِيَّمَا</foreign>:]) but this rendering is invalidated in such a phrase as <foreign lang="ar">وَلَا سِيَّمَا زَيْدٌ</foreign> by the supression of the correlative of the noun in the nom. case where there is no lengthiness, and by the applying <foreign lang="ar">ما</foreign> to denote a rational being: (Mughnee:) or you may put the noun after it in the gen. case, making <foreign lang="ar">ما</foreign> redundant, and making <foreign lang="ar">سِىّ</foreign> to govern the noun in that case because the meaning of <foreign lang="ar">سِىّ</foreign> is <foreign lang="ar">مِثْل</foreign>: [and this is the preferable way:] (Mughnee:) in both of these ways is recited the saying of Imra-el-Keys, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">أَلَا رُبَّ يُوْمٍ لَكَ مِنْهُنَّ صَالِحٍ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">وَلَا سِيَّمَا يَوْمٌٍ بِدَارَةِ جُلْجُلِ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">Verily many a good day was there to thee by reason of them; but there was not the like of a day,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">above all a day,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">especially a day, at Dárat Juljul,</hi> a certain pool, where Imra-el-Keys surprised his beloved, 'Oneyzeh, with others, her companions, bathing: see EM pp. 9 and 10]: you say also, <foreign lang="ar">أَضْرِبُ القَوْمَ وَلَا سِيَّمَا أَخِيكَ</foreign>, meaning <foreign lang="ar">وَلَا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">مِثْلَ ضَرْبِ أَخِيكَ</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">I will beat the people,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">party, but there shall not be the like of the beating of thy brother</hi>]: and if you say, <foreign lang="ar">وَلَا سِيَّمَا أَخُوكَ</foreign>, the meaning is, <foreign lang="ar">وَلَا مِثْلَ الَّذِى هُوَ أَخُوكَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">and there shall not be the like of him who is thy brother</hi>]: in the saying <foreign lang="ar">إِنَّ فُلَانًا كَرِيمٌ وَلَا سِيَّمَا إِنْ أَتَيْتَهُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">قَاعِدًا</foreign>, accord. to Akh, <foreign lang="ar">ما</foreign> is a substitute for the affixed pronoun <foreign lang="ar">هُ</foreign>, which is suppressed; the meaning being, <foreign lang="ar">وَلَا مِثْلَهُ إِنْ أَتَيْتَهُ قَاعِدًا</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">Verily such a one is generous, and there is not the like of him if thou come to him sitting</hi>]: (S, TA:) it is said in the Msb, [after explaining that <foreign lang="ar">ما</foreign> in <foreign lang="ar">سيّما</foreign> may be redundant, and the noun after it governed in the gen. case as the complement of a prefixed noun; and that <foreign lang="ar">ما</foreign> may be used in the sense of <foreign lang="ar">الّذى</foreign>, and the noun following put in the nom. case as the enunciative of the inchoative <foreign lang="ar">هو</foreign> which is suppressed;] that, accord. to some, the noun following may be in the accus. case, as being preceded by an exceptive; [or, as a specificative; (Mughnee;) in which case we must regard <foreign lang="ar">ما</foreign> as a substitute for the affixed pronoun <foreign lang="ar">هُ</foreign>;] <pb n="1479"/> but that this is not a good way; [and in this case, accord. to the generality of the authorities, it must be an indeterminate noun, not, like <foreign lang="ar">زَيْدٌ</foreign>, determinate: (Mughnee:)] also that <foreign lang="ar">سيّما</foreign> should not be used without <foreign lang="ar">لا</foreign> preceding it: and that it denotes the predominance of what follows it over what precedes it: but it is added that <foreign lang="ar">لا</foreign> is sometimes suppressed [as is said in the Mughnee] because known to be meant, though this is rare. (TA.) One says also, <foreign lang="ar">لَاسِىَّ لِمَا فُلَانٌ</foreign> (Lh, M, K) i. e. <hi rend="ital">There is not the like of such a one:</hi> (TA:) and <foreign lang="ar">لَا سِيَّكَ مَا فُلَانٌ</foreign> (Lh, M, K) i. e. <hi rend="ital">Such a one is not the like of thee.</hi> (TA.) [In both of these instances, <foreign lang="ar">ما</foreign> is obviously redundant. (Mgh.) It is said in a trad., <foreign lang="ar">فَأَمَرَ بِالخِرَبِ فَسُوِّيَتْ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">And he gave orders respecting the ruins, and they were levelled</hi>].                   <hi rend="ital">They were,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, equal in respect of the property, none of them exceeding another;</hi> as also <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n21350-4" target="اِسْتَوَوْا" n="4" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>فِيهِ</foreign>. (Msb.) It is said in a trad., as some relate it,   
      <foreign lang="ar">مَنْ <ref cref="n21350-5" target="سَاوَى" n="5" lang="ar" type="7" subtype="WOTF"/> يَوْمَاهُ فَهُوَ مَغْبُونٌ</foreign>, in which the meaning is said to be <foreign lang="ar">تَسَاوَى</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">He whose two days are alike,</hi> neither being distinguished above the other by any good done by him, <hi rend="ital">is weak-minded</hi>].                   <foreign lang="ar">تَفَاضَلُوا فَإِذَا تَسَاوَوْا هَلَكُوا</foreign>, (S, * TA,) i. e. [<hi rend="ital">Men will not cease to be in a good state while they vie in excellence,</hi>] <hi rend="ital">but when they cease from vying in excellent qualities and are content with defect</hi> [<hi rend="ital">and thus become alike, they perish</hi>]: or <hi rend="ital">when they become equal in ignorance:</hi> or <hi rend="ital">when they form themselves into parties and divisions, and every one is alone in his opinion, and they do not agree to acknowledge one exemplar</hi> or <hi rend="ital">chief</hi> or <hi rend="ital">leader</hi> [<hi rend="ital">so that they are all alike</hi>]: or, accord. to Az, <hi rend="ital">when they are alike in evil, there being none among them possessed of good.</hi> (TA.)    </entryFree>38:T3099,<entryFree id="n21351" key="استوى" type="main">

                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">سَوَآءٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> [in some copies of the K erroneously written without <foreign lang="ar">ء</foreign>] in its primary acceptation is an inf. n., [but without a proper verb, used as a simple subst.,] meaning <hi rend="ital">Equality, equability, uniformity,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">evenness;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">اِسْتِوَآءٌ</foreign>; (Mughnee;) as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n21357-1" target="سَوِيَّةٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n21361"/></foreign>: (M, K:) or [rather] it is a subst., (S, and Ksh and Bd in ii. 5,) meaning <foreign lang="ar">اِسْتِوَآءٌ</foreign>, (Ksh and Bd ibid.,) from <foreign lang="ar">اِسْتَوَى</foreign> in the sense of <foreign lang="ar">اِعْتَدَلَ</foreign>; (S;) and signifies [as above: and] <hi rend="ital">equity, justice,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">rectitude;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">عَدْلٌ</foreign>; (S, M, K;) as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n21357-2" target="سَوِيَّةً" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>; (M;) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n21357-3" target="سِوًى" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n21356"/></foreign> and

                  <hi rend="ital">The night of the thirteenth</hi> [<hi rend="ital">of the lunar month;</hi> the first being that on which the new moon is first seen]; (As, S, K, TA;) <hi rend="ital">in which the moon becomes equable</hi> or <hi rend="ital">uniform</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">يَسْتَوِى</foreign>) [<hi rend="ital">in illumination</hi>]: (TA:) or <hi rend="ital">the night of the fourteenth.</hi> (M, K.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  And <hi rend="ital">i. q.</hi>

                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">سَوَاسِيَةٌ كَأَسْنَانِ الحِمَارِ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">Equals like the teeth of the ass</hi>]. (TA.) It requires two [or more nouns for its subjects]: you say, <foreign lang="ar">سَوَآءٌ زَيْدٌ وَعَمْرٌو</foreign>, meaning <foreign lang="ar">ذَوَا سَوَآءٍ</foreign> [i. e., lit., <hi rend="ital">Two possessors of equality,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">likeness, are Zeyd and 'Amr</hi>], (M, K,) because it is [originally] an inf. n.: (M:) and <foreign lang="ar">هُمَا فِى هٰذَا الأَمْرِ سَوَآءٌ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">They two are in this affair,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">case, likes</hi>]: (S:) and <foreign lang="ar">هُمَا سَوَاآنِ</foreign> (S, M, K) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n21357-41" target="سِيَّانِ" n="41" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> i. e. <hi rend="ital">They two are likes:</hi> (S, M, Mgh, Msb, K:) and <foreign lang="ar">هُمْ سَوَآءٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">أَسْوَآءٌ</foreign> and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n21357-42" target="سَوَاسِيَةٌ" n="42" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> i. e. <hi rend="ital">They are likes;</hi> (S; [the first and last of these three are mentioned in the Mgh as identical in meaning;]) or, accord. to Fr, the last means <hi rend="ital">they are equals in evil,</hi> not in good: (T, TA:) and   
      <foreign lang="ar">مَاهُوَ لَكَ <ref cref="n21357-43" target="بِسِىٍّ" n="43" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He is not a person like to thee:</hi> and <foreign lang="ar">مَاهُمْ لَكَ بِأَسْوَآءٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">They are not persons like to thee</hi>]: (Lh, M:) and   
      <foreign lang="ar">مَاهِىَ لَكَ <ref cref="n21357-44" target="بِسِىٍّ" n="44" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> (Lh, M, K *) i. e. <hi rend="ital">She is not a person like to thee:</hi> (TA:) and <foreign lang="ar">مَاهُنَّ لَكَ بِأَسْوَآءٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">They</hi> (females) <hi rend="ital">are not persons like to thee</hi>]: and <foreign lang="ar">لَا <ref cref="n21357-45" target="سِىَّ" n="45" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>لِمَنْ فَعَلَ ذَاكَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">There is not a like to him who did that</hi>]: and <foreign lang="ar">لَا <ref cref="n21357-46" target="سِيَّكَ" n="46" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>إِذَا فَعَلْتَ ذَاكَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">There is not the like of thee when thou doest that</hi>]: (Lh, M, K:) and <foreign lang="ar">لَا <ref cref="n21357-47" target="سِيَّةَ" n="47" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>فُلَانٍ</foreign> (K) [<hi rend="ital">There is not the like of such a one:</hi> in the CK, <foreign lang="ar">فُلَانٌ</foreign>: perhaps the right reading is <foreign lang="ar">لَا <ref cref="n21357-48" target="سِيَّكَ" n="48" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>فُلَانٌ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Such a one is not the like of thee</hi>]. <foreign lang="ar">سَوَآءٌ</foreign> and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n21357-49" target="سِيَّانِ" n="49" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> should not be used with <foreign lang="ar">أَوْ</foreign> in the place of <foreign lang="ar">وَ</foreign> except by poetic license: one of the exceptions to this rule is the saying of Aboo-Dhu-eyb, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">وَكَانَ سِيَّانِ أَلَّا يَسْرَحُوا نَعَمًا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">أَوْ يَسْرَحُوهُ بِهَا وَٱغْبَرَّتِ السُّوحُ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">And they were two like cases that they should not send forth cattle to pasture or send him forth with them when the tracts were very dusty</hi> by reason of drought]. (M.) For two other exs. of <foreign lang="ar">سَوَآء</foreign>, [as well as of its syn. <foreign lang="ar">سِىّ</foreign>, and for <foreign lang="ar">لَا سِيَّمَا</foreign> also,] see <foreign lang="ar">سِىٌّ</foreign>.          <sense type="b" n="7">-b7-</sense>  See also <foreign lang="ar">سِوًى</foreign> in six places.    </entryFree>3b:T6bc,<entryFree id="n21361" key="سَوِيَّةٌ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">سَوِيَّةٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>: see <foreign lang="ar">سَوَآءٌ</foreign>, in five places.          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  [Also fem. of <foreign lang="ar">سَوِىٌّ</foreign>.          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  And hence, as a subst.,] <hi rend="ital">A kind of vehicle of female slaves and of necessitous persons:</hi> (K:) or <hi rend="ital">a</hi> [<hi rend="ital">garment of the kind called</hi>] <foreign lang="ar">كِسَآء</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">stuffed with panic grass</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">ثُمَام</foreign>), (S, M, K, and L in art. <foreign lang="ar">كرب</foreign>,) or <hi rend="ital">palm-fibres</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">لِيف</foreign>), (M,) or <hi rend="ital">the like,</hi> (S, M, and L ubi suprà,) <hi rend="ital">resembling the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بَرْذَعَة</foreign> [q. v.], (S, and L ubi suprà,) <hi rend="ital">which is put on the back of the camel,</hi> (M,) or <hi rend="ital">on the back of the ass &amp;c.,</hi> (L ubi suprà,) <hi rend="ital">and which is one of the vehicles of female slaves and of necessitous persons:</hi> (M:) and likewise <hi rend="ital">such as is put upon the back of the camel, but in the form of a ring because of the hump, and</hi> [<hi rend="ital">also</hi>] <hi rend="ital">called</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">حَوِيَّةٌ</foreign> [q. v.]: pl. <foreign lang="ar">سَوَايَا</foreign>. (S.)    </entryFree>3c:T46e,<entryFree id="n21367" key="مُسْوٍ" type="main">

One says in answer to him who asks, “ How have ye entered upon the morning? ” (S,) or “ How have ye entered upon the evening? ” (M, TA,) <foreign lang="ar">مُسْوُونَ صَالِحُونَ</foreign> [as [as enunciatives of <foreign lang="ar">أَصْبَحْنَا</foreign> or <foreign lang="ar">أَمْسَيْنَا</foreign> understood, but I think that <foreign lang="ar">مُسْتَوِينَ</foreign> is a mistranscription for <foreign lang="ar">مُسْوِينَ</foreign>], meaning <hi rend="ital">In a good, right, state, with respect to our children and our cattle.</hi> (S, M, TA.)
